ADOPTING ORDINANCES
ORDINANCE NO. 001-2010
   AN ORDINANCE ENACTING A CODE OF ORDINANCES FOR THE VILLAGE OF GARDNER
REVISING, AMENDING, RESTATING, CODIFYING AND COMPILING EXISTING GENERAL
ORDINANCES OF THE VILLAGE OF GARDNER, AND ADOPTING CERTAIN ZONING TEXT
AMENDMENTS
   WHEREAS, the present general and permanent ordinances of the Village of
Gardner are inadequately arranged and classified and are insufficient in form
and substance for the complete preservation of the public peace, health, safety
and general welfare of the municipality and for the proper conduct of its
affairs; and
   WHEREAS, the Acts of the Legislature of the State of Illinois empower and
authorize the Village of Gardner as set forth therein to revise, amend,
restate, codify and compile any existing ordinances and all new ordinances not
heretofore adopted or published and to incorporate such ordinances into one
ordinance in book form; and
   WHEREAS, the Village of Gardner has authorized a general compilation,
revision and codification of the ordinances of the Village of Gardner of a
general and permanent nature and publication of such ordinance in book form;
and
   WHEREAS, a Public Hearing was properly noticed and held before the Village
of Gardner Planning & Zoning Board on Tuesday, April 6, 2010, at 7:00 p.m.,
with due notice having been published; and
   WHEREAS, following the above Public Hearing, the Gardner Planning & Zoning
Board unanimously recommended the adoption of the zoning text amendments
associated with the codification of the ordinances of the Village of Gardner. 
A true and correct copy of the Findings and Recommendation of the Gardner
Planning & Zoning Board is attached hereto as Exhibit A and incorporated
herein; and
   WHEREAS, after due consideration, the Gardner Village Council finds that it
would be in the best interests of the residents of the Village of Gardner to
follow the recommendations of the Gardner Planning & Zoning Board, and to
approve the zoning text amendments.
   NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED BY THE MAYOR AND VILLAGE COUNCIL OF THE
VILLAGE OF GARDNER, GRUNDY COUNTY, ILLINOIS, AS FOLLOWS:
   Section 1.   The above recitals are hereby found to be true and correct, and
are hereby restated and incorporated into the body of this ordinance as though
fully set forth herein.
   Section 2.   The general ordinances of the Village of Gardner as revised,
amended, restated, codified and compiled in book form are hereby adopted as and
shall constitute the “Code of Ordinances of the Village of Gardner, Grundy
County, Illinois.”  Said general ordinances are hereby incorporated into the
body of this ordinance as though fully set forth herein.
   Section 3.   The zoning text amendments considered by the Planning & Zoning
Board and recommended for approval are hereby approved and ratified in all
respects.
   Section 4.   Such Code of Ordinances as adopted in Section 1 shall consist
of the following Titles:
   VILLAGE OF GARDNER, ILLINOIS
   CODE OF ORDINANCES
   TABLE OF CONTENTS
         TITLE I:  GENERAL PROVISIONS
         TITLE III:  ADMINISTRATION
         TITLE V:  PUBLIC WORKS
         TITLE VII:  TRAFFIC CODE
         TITLE IX:  GENERAL REGULATIONS
         TITLE XI:  BUSINESS REGULATIONS
         TITLE XIII:  GENERAL OFFENSES
         TITLE XV:  LAND USAGE
         TABLE OF SPECIAL ORDINANCES
         PARALLEL REFERENCES
         INDEX
   Section 5.   All prior ordinances pertaining to the subjects treated in such
Code of Ordinances shall be deemed repealed from and after the effective date
of this ordinance except as they are included and re-ordained in whole or in
part in such Code; provided, such repeal shall not affect any offense committed
or penalty incurred or any right established prior to the effective date of
this ordinance, nor shall such repeal affect the provisions of ordinances
levying taxes, appropriating money, annexing or detaching territory,
establishing franchises, or granting special rights to certain persons,
authorizing public improvements, authorizing the issuance of bonds or borrowing
of money, authorizing the purchase or sale of real or personal property,
granting or accepting easements, plat or dedication of land to public use,
vacating or setting the boundaries of streets or other public places; nor shall
such repeal affect any other ordinance of a temporary or special nature or
pertaining to subjects not contained in or covered by the Code.
   Section 6.   Such Code shall be deemed published as of the day of its
adoption by the Gardner Village Council, and the Gardner Village Clerk is
hereby authorized and directed to file a copy of such Code of Ordinances in the
Office of the Clerk.
   Section 7.   Such Code shall be effective from and following its approval
and publication in pamphlet form as required by law.
   Section 8.   The Village Clerk shall publish a true, correct and complete
copy of the Code of Ordinances immediately from and following its approval for
a period of not less than ten (10) days and shall complete a Certificate of
Posting Consistent therewith.
   PASSED AND ADOPTED by the Gardner Village Council on this 12th day of April,
2010.
Ayes:   5

§ 1.05.005  TITLE OF CODE.
   This codification by and for the Village of Gardner shall be designated as
the Code of Gardner and may be so cited.
§ 1.05.010  DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this code, the following definitions shall apply unless
the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ANOTHER.  When used to designate the owner of property which is the subject
of an offense, includes not only natural persons, but also every other owner of
property.
   CITY and TOWN.  Each mean the Village of Gardner, Illinois, or the area
within the territorial limits of the Village of Gardner, Illinois, and the
territory outside of the village over which the village has jurisdiction or
control by virtue of any constitutional or statutory provision.
   COUNCIL or VILLAGE COUNCIL.  The Council of the Village of Gardner.
   COUNTY. Grundy County, Illinois.
   COUNTY BOARD.  The County Board of Grundy County, Illinois.
(5 ILCS 70/1.07)
   COURT.  Construed to mean any court of competent jurisdiction.
   DECREE.  Synonymous with JUDGMENT. 
(5 ILCS 70/1.24)
   ELECTORS.  Persons qualified to vote for elective officers at municipal
elections. 
(65 ILCS 5/1-1-2)
   EXECUTIVE OFFICER.  Words used for an executive or ministerial officer may
include any deputy or other person performing the duties of the officer, either
generally or in special cases. 
(5 ILCS 70/1.08)
   HERETOFORE or HEREAFTER.  HERETOFORE means any time previous to the day on
which the ordinance, resolution or statute takes effect; HEREAFTER means at any
time after that date. 
(5 ILCS 70/1.17)
   HIGHWAY,ROAD or STREET.  May include any road laid out by authority of the
United States, or of this state, or of any town or county of this state, and
all bridges thereupon.
(5 ILCS 70/1.16)
   ILCS.  Illinois Compiled Statutes, 1992, as heretofore and hereafter
amended.
   KEEPER or PROPRIETOR.  Includes all persons, whether acting by themselves,
or as a servant, agent or employee.
   LAND or REAL ESTATE.  Includes rights and easements of an incorporeal
nature.
   LAW.  Denotes applicable federal law, the Constitution and statutes of the
State of Illinois, the ordinances of the Village of Gardner, and, when
appropriate, any and all rules and regulations which may be promulgated
thereunder.
   MAY.  The act referred to is permissive.
   MAYOR.  The Mayor of the Village of Gardner.
   MONTH.  A calendar month. 
(5 ILCS 70/1.10)
   MUNICIPAL CODE.  The Illinois Municipal Code, 65 ILCS 5.
   MUST and SHALL.  Are each mandatory.
   OATH.  Includes affirmation, and SWEAR includes affirm.
(5 ILCS 70/1.12)
   OWNER.  When applied to property, includes any part owner, joint owner,
purchaser and seller under a contract and/or deed, or tenant in common of the
whole or part of the property, and includes any beneficiary of a land trust
which owns property.
   PERSON.  Any legal person; includes associations, partnerships,
corporations, joint ventures and bodies politic and corporate as well as
individuals.  (5 ILCS 70/1.05)
   PERSONAL PROPERTY.  Includes all property except real.
   POLICE OFFICERS.
      (1)   Police officers employed and in the service of the Village of
Gardner.
      (2)   POLICE FORCE shall be construed to include such persons in the
employ of a village as members of the Department of Police, who are or shall
hereafter be appointed and sworn as POLICE OFFICERS.
(5 ILCS 70/1.20)
   PROCEEDING and FOLLOWING.  Next before and next after, respectively.
   PREMISES.  As applied to property, includes land and buildings.
   PROPERTY.  Includes real, personal, mixed estates and other interests.
   PUBLIC AUTHORITY.  Includes school districts; units of legal government; the
village, county, state or federal governments, officers and agencies thereof,
or any commissions or committees thereof; or any duly authorized public
official.
   PUBLIC PLACE.  Includes any street, sidewalk, park, cemetery, school yard,
body of water or watercourse, public conveyance or any other place for the sale
of merchandise, public accommodation or amusement.
   REAL PROPERTY.  Includes lands, tenements and hereditaments.
   REGISTERED MAIL.  Includes certified mail and CERTIFIED MAIL includes
registered mail.
   SHALL.  The act referred to is mandatory.
   SIDEWALK.  The portion of the street between the curb lines, or the lateral
lines of a roadway, and the adjacent property lines, intended for use of
pedestrians.
(625 ILCS 5/1.188)
   SPECIAL DISTRICTS.  The meaning ascribed in Article VII of the Constitution
of the State of Illinois of 1970. 
(5 ILCS 70/1.29)
   STATE.  The State of Illinois.
   STREET.  Where the context admits, includes alleys, lanes, courts,
boulevards, squares and other public thoroughfares.
   TENANT or OCCUPANT.  As applied to premises, includes any person holding a
written or oral lease, or who actually occupies the whole or any part of the
premises, alone or with others.
   THIS CODE or THIS CODE OF ORDINANCES.  The village code hereby adopted, and
as hereinafter modified by amendment, revision and by the adoption of new
titles, chapters or sections.
   UNITS OF LOCAL GOVERNMENT.  The meaning established in § 1 of Article VII of
the Constitution of the State of Illinois of 1970. 
(5 ILCS 70/1.28)
   VILLAGE, MUNICIPALITY or MUNICIPAL CORPORATION.  The Village of Gardner,
irrespective of its population or legal classification.
   WEEK.  Seven consecutive days.
   WHOEVER.  Includes all persons, natural and artificial; partners;
principals, agents and employees; and all officials, public or private.
   WRITTEN or IN WRITING.  Includes printing, electronic  and any other mode of
representing words and letters; but when the written signature of any person is
required by law on any official or public writing or bond, required by law, it
shall be:
      (1)   In the proper handwriting of that person, or in case he or she is
unable to write, his or her proper mark; or
      (2)   An electronic signature as defined in the Electronic Commerce
Security Act, 5 ILCS 175/1-101 et seq., except as otherwise provided by law.
(5 ILCS 70/1.15)
   YEAR.  A calendar year unless otherwise expressed; and the word YEAR alone
is equivalent to the expression “Year of Our Lord”.
(5 ILCS 70/1.10)
§ 1.05.015  SECTION HEADINGS.
   Headings and captions used in this code are employed for reference purposes
only and shall not be deemed a part of the text of any section.
§ 1.05.020  RULES OF CONSTRUCTION.
   (A)   Words and phrases shall be read in context and construed according to
the rules of grammar and common usage. Words and phrases that have acquired a
technical or particular meaning, whether by legislative or judicial definition
or otherwise, shall be construed accordingly.
   (B)   As used in this code, unless the context otherwise requires, the
following rules will be followed.
      (1)   The singular shall include the plural and the plural shall include
the singular. 
(5 ILCS 70/1.03)
      (2)   Words of one gender shall include the other genders.
(5 ILCS 70/1.04)
      (3)   Words in the present tense shall include the future.
(5 ILCS 70/1.02)
      (4)   AND may be read OR, and OR may be read AND, if the context admits.
   (C)   The time within which any act provided by law is to be done shall be
computed by excluding the first day and including the last, unless the last day
is Saturday or Sunday or is a holiday as defined or fixed in any statute now or
hereafter in force in this state, and then it shall also be excluded. If the
day succeeding Saturday, Sunday or a holiday is also a holiday or a Saturday or
Sunday, then the succeeding day shall also be excluded. 
(5 ILCS 70/1.11)
   (D)   When the law requires an act to be done which may by law as well be
done by an agent as by the principal, the requirement shall be construed to
include all the acts when done by an authorized agent.
   (E)   Words purporting to give joint authority to three or more municipal
officers or other persons shall be construed as giving authority to a majority
of the officers or persons. 
(5 ILCS 70/1.09)
   (F)   These rules of construction shall not apply to any provision of this
code which shall contain any express provision excluding that construction, or
when the subject matter or context of this code may be repugnant thereto.
   (G)   All general provisions, terms, phrases and expressions shall be
liberally construed in order that the true intent and meaning of the Mayor and
Village Council may be fully carried out. 
(5 ILCS 70/1.01)
   (H)   The provisions of any ordinance, in so far as they are the same as
those of any prior ordinance, shall be construed as a continuation of the prior
provisions, and not as a new enactment. 
(5 ILCS 70/2)
§ 1.05.025  OFFICIAL TIME.
   The official time for the village shall be as set by federal law.
§ 1.05.030  REVIVOR; EFFECT OF AMENDMENT OR REPEAL.
   (A)   The repeal of a repealing ordinance does not revive the ordinance
originally repealed, nor impair the effect of any saving clause therein.
   (B)   The reenactment, amendment or repeal of an ordinance does not do any
of the following, except as provided in division (C) below:
      (1)   Affect the prior operation of the ordinance or any prior action
taken thereunder;
      (2)   Affect any validation, cure, right, privilege, obligation or
liability previously acquired, accrued, accorded or incurred thereunder;
      (3)   Affect any violation thereof or penalty, forfeiture or punishment
incurred in respect thereto, prior to the amendment or repeal; or
      (4)   Affect any investigation, proceeding or remedy in respect of any
privilege, obligation, liability, penalty, forfeiture or punishment. The
investigation, proceeding or remedy may be instituted, continued or enforced,
and the penalty, forfeiture or punishment imposed, as if the ordinance had not
been repealed or amended.
   (C)   If the penalty, forfeiture or punishment for any offense is reduced by
a reenactment or amendment of an ordinance, the penalty, forfeiture or
punishment, if not already imposed, shall be imposed according to the ordinance
as amended.
§ 1.05.035  REFERENCE TO OTHER SECTIONS.
   (A)   Wherever in a penalty section reference is made to a violation of a
section or an inclusive group of sections, the reference shall be construed to
mean a violation of any provision of the section or sections included in the
reference.
   (B)   References in this code to action taken or authorized under designated
sections of this code include, in every case, action taken or authorized under
the applicable legislative provision which is superseded by this code.
   (C)   Whenever in one section reference is made to another section hereof,
the reference shall extend and apply to the section referred to as subsequently
amended, revised, recodified or renumbered unless the subject matter is changed
or materially altered by the amendment or revision and the context clearly
indicates that the reference to the section as amended or revised was not
intended.
§ 1.05.040  CONFLICTING PROVISIONS.
   If the provisions of different codes, chapters or sections of these codified
ordinances conflict with or contravene each other, the provisions bearing the
latest passage date shall prevail. If the conflicting provisions bear the same
passage date, the conflict shall be construed so as to be consistent with the
meaning or legal effect of the questions of the subject matter taken as a
whole.
§ 1.05.045  AMENDMENTS TO CODE.
   All ordinances passed subsequent to this code which amend, repeal or in any
way affect this code may be numbered in accordance with the numbering system of
this code and printed for inclusion herein, or in the case of repealed
chapters, sections and divisions, or any part thereof, by subsequent
ordinances, the repealed portions may be excluded from the code by the omission
from reprinted pages affected thereby, and the subsequent ordinances as
numbered and printed or omitted, in the case of repeal, shall be prima facie
evidence of subsequent ordinances until this code of ordinances and subsequent
ordinances numbered or omitted are re-adopted as a new code of ordinances by
the Village Council.
§ 1.05.050  SEVERABILITY.
   If any provisions of a section of these codified ordinances or the
application thereof to any person or circumstance is held invalid, the
invalidity shall not affect other provisions or applications of the section or
related sections which can be given effect without the invalid provision or
application, and to this end the provisions are severable.
§ 1.05.055  REFERENCE TO PUBLIC OFFICE OR OFFICER.
   (A)   Reference to a public office or officer shall be deemed to apply to
any office, officer or employee of the village exercising the powers, duties or
functions contemplated in the provision, irrespective of any transfer of
functions or change in the official title of the functionary.
   (B)   The references shall also include the designee or agent of any officer
or office, unless the law or the context clearly requires otherwise.
§ 1.05.060  ERRORS AND OMISSIONS.
   (A)   If a manifest error is discovered consisting of the misspelling of any
word or words, the omission of any word or words necessary to express the
intention of the provisions affected, the use of a word or words to which no
meaning can be attached or the use of a word or words when another word or
words was clearly intended to express the intent, the spelling shall be
corrected, and the word or words supplied, omitted or substituted as will
conform with the manifest intention, and the provision shall have the same
effect as though the correct words were contained in the text as originally
published.
   (B)   No alteration shall be made or permitted if any question exists
regarding the nature or extent of the error.
§ 1.05.065  ORDINANCES REPEALED.
   (A)   This code, from and after its effective date, shall contain all of the
provisions of a general nature pertaining to the subjects herein enumerated and
embraced.
   (B)   All prior ordinances pertaining to the subjects addressed by this code
which are inconsistent with the provisions of this code, or any portions
thereof, shall be deemed repealed and revoked from and after the effective date
of this code of ordinances to the extent of any inconsistencies.
§ 1.05.070  ORDINANCES UNAFFECTED.
   All ordinances of a temporary or special nature (including, but not limited
to, tax levy ordinances; appropriation ordinances; ordinances relating to
boundaries and annexations; franchise ordinances and other ordinances granting
special rights to persons or corporations; contract ordinances and ordinances
authorizing the execution of a contract or the issuance of warrants; salary
ordinances; ordinances establishing, naming or vacating streets, alleys or
other public places; improvement ordinances; bond ordinances; ordinances
relating to elections; ordinances relating to the transfer or acceptance of
real estate by or from the village and all special ordinances) as well as any
other ordinances pertaining to subjects not enumerated and embraced in this
code of ordinances, shall remain in full force and effect unless herein
repealed expressly or by necessary implication.
§ 1.05.075  ORDINANCES SAVED.
   Whenever an ordinance by its nature either authorizes or enables the Village
Council or a certain village officer or employee to make additional regulations
for the purpose of carrying out the intent of the ordinance, all regulations of
a similar nature serving that purpose effected prior to the codification and
not inconsistent thereto, shall remain in effect and are saved.
§ 1.05.080  TECHNICAL CODES.
   Whenever any technical codes are incorporated herein by reference, any
subsequent amendments or revisions to the technical codes shall automatically
become a part of this code and shall be made available for public inspection by
the village. Further, to the extent of any conflict between the technical
provisions of this code and any technical codes adopted by reference, the most
restrictive provision shall prevail.
§ 1.05.085  HISTORICAL AND STATUTORY REFERENCES.
   (A)   As histories for the code sections, the specific number and passage
date of the original ordinance, and the amending ordinances, if any, are listed
following the text of the code section.  Example:  (Ord. 10, passed 5-13-1960;
Ord. 15, passed 1-1-1970; Ord. 20, passed 1-1-1980; Ord. 25, passed 1-1-1985)
   (B)   (1)   An “ILCS” cite included in the history indicates that the text
of the section reads either verbatim or substantially the same as the statute. 
Example:  (65 ILCS 5/3.1-2-1)
      (2)   An “ILCS” cite set forth as a “statutory reference” following the
text of the section indicates that the reader should refer to that statute for
further information.  Example:
   § 3.10.100  PUBLIC RECORDS AVAILABLE.
   The village shall make available to any person for inspection or copying all
public records, as provided in the Illinois Freedom of Information Act.
   Statutory reference:
      Freedom of Information Act, see 5 ILCS 140/1 et seq.
§ 1.05.090  TITLE OF OFFICE.
   Use of the title of any officer, employee, department, board or commission
means that officer, employee, department, board or commission of the village.
(Prior Code, § 1.04.020)
§ 1.05.095  INTERPRETATION OF LANGUAGE.
   All words and phrases shall be construed according to the common and
approved usage of the language, but technical words and phrases and the others
as may have acquired a peculiar and appropriate meaning in the law shall be
construed and understood according to the peculiar and appropriate meaning.
(Prior Code, § 1.04.030)
§ 1.05.100  PROHIBITED ACTS INCLUDE CAUSING AND PERMITTING.
   Whenever, in the ordinances of the village, any act or omission is made
unlawful, it shall include causing, allowing, permitting, aiding, abetting,
suffering or concealing the fact of the act or omission.
(Prior Code, § 1.04.060)
§ 1.05.105  COMPUTATION OF TIME.
   Except when otherwise provided, the time within which an act is required to
be done shall be computed by excluding the first day and including the last
day, unless the last day is Sunday or a holiday, in which case it shall also be
excluded.
(Prior Code, § 1.04.070)
§ 1.05.110  CONSTRUCTION.
   The provisions of the ordinances of the village, and all proceedings under
them, are to be construed with a view to effect their objects and to promote
justice.
(Prior Code, § 1.04.080)
§ 1.05.115  ELECTIONS; PROCEDURES.
   All elections of village officers shall be conducted in accordance with the
provisions of 65 ILCS 5/4-3-1 et seq.
(Prior Code, § 1.16.010)
§ 1.05.120  MUNICIPAL YEAR.
   The municipal year of the village shall commence with May 1 and end with
April 30, in each calendar year.
(Prior Code, § 1.20.010)
§ 1.05.125  FISCAL YEAR.
   The fiscal year of the village shall commence with May 1 and end with April
30, in each calendar year.
(Prior Code, § 1.20.020)
§ 1.05.130  STYLE.
   The style of all ordinances enacted by the Mayor and Council of the village
shall be:
      “Be it ordained by the Mayor and Council of the Village of Gardner,
Illinois”.
(Prior Code, § 1.24.010)
§ 1.05.135  PUBLICATION.
   All ordinances enacted by the Council of the Village of Gardner shall be
published, if necessary, in accordance with the applicable statutes of the
State of Illinois then in force, and as may be amended from time to time.
(Prior Code, § 1.24.020)
§ 1.05.140  MANNER OF ENACTMENT.
   (A)   Upon every vote the “yeas” and “nays” shall be called and recorded.
   (B)   Every ordinance or resolution appropriating any money, or ordering any
street improvement or sewer or making or authorizing the making of any
contract, or granting any franchise, right or license to occupy or use the
streets, alleys, highways, bridges, viaducts, public property or public places
in the municipality for any purpose shall remain on file with the Municipal
Clerk for public inspection, in the form in which it is finally passed, at
least one week before the final passage thereof.
(Prior Code, § 1.24.030)
§ 1.05.145  AUTHENTICATION; CERTIFICATION.
   The contents of all ordinances, including the date of passage and the date
of publication or posting, where required, may be authenticated by the Village
Clerk by executing a certification of the ordinance by the Village Clerk, under
the seal of the village.
(Prior Code, § 1.24.040)
§ 1.05.150  SIGNING AND FILING.
   Every resolution, ordinance or warrant passed or ordered by the Village
Council shall be signed by the Mayor or by two Commissioners, and all
ordinances and resolutions shall be filed with the Village Clerk for record,
before they shall be in force.
(Prior Code, § 1.24.050)
§ 1.05.155  VILLAGE OF GARDNER P-TICKET ENFORCEMENT PROGRAM.
   (A)   The Village of Gardner hereby creates an enforcement vehicle which
shall be known as the “P-Ticket” for the enforcement of certain ordinances.
Persons who are issued a “P-Ticket” by appropriate village agents and employees
shall be given the option of tendering a written plea of guilty along with
payment of the fine set herein, and as hereafter amended, directly to the
Village Clerk within 14 days of the issuance of “P-Ticket”. Persons who do not
pay the fine and enter a plea of guilty within the given 14 days with the
Village Clerk of the Village of Gardner shall be subject to summons to hearing
in the Circuit Court and shall be subject to the full range of fines and
penalties as provided by each separate village ordinance.
   (B)   “P-Tickets” shall not be issued to any one person who has been
convicted or plead guilty to any one of the offenses enumerated on the “P-
Ticket” three or more times in the past or any single time within a 12-month
period.
   (C)   A “P-Ticket” shall be issued at the discretion of the village for
violations of the following titles, chapters, subchapters, amendments and
ordinances thereto:
      (1)   Title XI: Business Licenses and Regulations;
      (2)   
Chapter 9.05: Animals;
      (3)   
Chapter 9.20: Health and Safety;
      (4)   
Chapter 13.10: Offenses Against Public Morals;
      (5)   Title V: Public Works;
      (6)   
Chapter 15.15: Zoning;
      (8)   
Chapter 9.20: Ordinance Prohibiting Certain Noises;
      (9)   Section
9.20.240: Ordinance Prohibiting Scavenging of Recyclable Materials From
Curbside Recycling Bins;
      (10)   
Chapter 7.25: Prohibiting Use of Skateboards and the Like; and
      (11)   
Chapter 13.10: Ordinance to Suppress Graffiti.
   (D)   The fines to be collected upon the plea of guilty of a person charged
with an ordinance violation by the “P-Ticket” method shall be $25.
   (E)   This section shall amend any existing ordinance inconsistent herewith.
This section shall take full force and effect upon its due passage, notice and
publication, as may be required by law.
(Ord. VG00-325, passed 5-8-2000)
§ 1.05.999  GENERAL PENALTY.
   Whoever violates any provision of this code or other ordinance of this
village for which another penalty is not specifically provided, shall be fined
not less than $75 and not more than $750 for each and every violation thereof,
and every day the violation continues shall constitute a separate offense.
Statutory reference:
   Authority to imprison for certain ordinance violations, see 65 ILCS 5/1-2-
1.1
   Limitations on penalties, see 65 ILCS 5/1-2-1
CHAPTER 1.10: VILLAGE BOUNDARIES AND SEAL
Section
Corporate Limits
   
1.10.005   Designated
Seal
   
1.10.050   Construction
   
1.10.055   Custody
CORPORATE LIMITS
§ 1.10.005  DESIGNATED.
   The corporate limits shall include all property shown on the official zoning
map of the village, as now existing and as later annexed or amended, according
to the applicable statutes of the state then in force. The Gardner Planning and
Zoning Board is authorized and directed by statute to review the Village of
Gardner Zoning Map at least annually of each year in March and to update the
same as may be necessary.
(Prior Code, § 1.08.010)
SEAL
§ 1.10.050  CONSTRUCTION.
   The corporate seal of the village shall be circular in form, and be so
constructed as to impress on paper in the center of the circle and the word
“SEAL”, surrounded by the words “Village of Gardner, Grundy County, Illinois”.
(Prior Code, § 1.12.010)
§ 1.10.055  CUSTODY.
   The seal shall be and remain in custody of the Village Clerk of the village,
and his or her successor in office, to be used by him or her in all cases
provided for by the ordinances of the village, or the laws of the state, and in
all other cases where, by the laws and customs of any state or nation, the use
of the corporate seal of the village becomes necessary.
(Prior Code, § 1.12.020)

OFFICERS
§ 3.05.005  ELECTED OFFICERS.
   (A)   The Village Council of the village shall consist of a Mayor and four
Commissioners, all of whom shall be elected to a term of four years. At the
first regular meeting following an election, the Council, by majority vote,
shall designate one Commissioner to be the Commissioner of each of the
following departments:
      (1)   Department of Accounts and Finances;
      (2)   Department of Public Health and Safety;
      (3)   Department of Streets and Public Improvement; and
      (4)   Department of Public Property.
   (B)   The Mayor shall serve as the Commissioner of the Department of Public
Affairs. Each Commissioner shall exercise the power and have the duties as set
forth in this title and as prescribed by statute.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.010)
§ 3.05.010  APPOINTED OFFICERS.
   (A)   At the first meeting following general election, or as soon thereafter
as is practicable, the Council, by majority vote may appoint the following
officers:
      (1)   Village Clerk;
      (2)   Village Attorney;
      (3)   Village Treasurer; and
      (4)   Village Engineer.
   (B)   From time to time thereafter, the Council may create, fill and
discontinue other officers in accordance with its judgment, the needs of the
municipality and consistent with Illinois law, as amended.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.020)
§ 3.05.015  SUBORDINATE DEPARTMENT HEADS.
   The Council has the right and power, by majority vote, to appoint and
discharge heads of all principal departments subordinate to those enumerated in
§
3.05.005.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.030)
§ 3.05.020  OATH IN OFFICE.
   Every officer of the village shall, before entering upon his or her duties,
take the oath prescribed by law.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.040)
§ 3.05.025  BOND.
   (A)   Before entering upon the duties of their respective offices, the
Mayor, each Commissioner and the Village Clerk shall execute bonds conditioned
upon the faithful performance of their duties, with good and sufficient
sureties approved by the Council, in the penal sum of $3,000.
   (B)   The Village Treasurer shall execute a bond conditioned upon the
faithful performance of his or her duties in an amount as prescribed by
statute.
   (C)   All bonds required by this section shall be filed as prescribed by
statute.
   (D)   The Council may from time to time by ordinance designate and direct
that additional officers and employees file bonds and may further designate the
amount of the bonds.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.050)
§ 3.05.030  SALARIES.
   (A)   The Mayor and Commissioners shall receive compensation only in the
manner provided by statute.
   (B)   All other officers and employees of the village shall receive the
salaries as may be provided from time to time by resolution of the Council.
   (C)   No officer or employee receiving a salary from the village shall be
entitled to retain any portion of any fees collected by him or her in the
performance of his or her duties as a municipal officer or employee in the
absence of a specific ordinance provision to that effect.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.060)
§ 3.05.035  POWER TO ARREST.
   The Mayor and Commissioners, as well as members of the Police Department,
are declared to be conservators of the peace with the powers to make arrests as
are given to the conservators of the peace by statute.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.070)
§ 3.05.040  TERMINATION OF OFFICE.
   Every officer of the village, upon the termination of his or her office, for
any cause whatsoever, shall deliver to his or her successor all books and
records which may be the property of the village; and if no successor has been
appointed within one week after the termination of office, the property shall
be delivered to the Clerk or to the Treasurer.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.080)
§ 3.05.045  IMPERSONATION UNLAWFUL.
   It is unlawful for any person to impersonate without lawful authority any
village officer or employee. Any person violating this section shall be fined
not less than $75 nor more than $750 for each offense.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.090)  Penalty, see §
3.05.999
MAYOR
§ 3.05.060  TERM.
   The Mayor shall serve until his or her successor is elected and qualified as
is provided by statute.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.010)
§ 3.05.065  DUTIES.
   The Mayor shall serve as president of the Council and preside at its
meetings, and he or she shall supervise all departments and report to the
Council for its action all matters requiring attention in any department.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.020)
§ 3.05.070  VOTING.
   The Mayor shall have the right to vote on all questions coming before the
Council.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.030)
§ 3.05.075  VETO.
   The Mayor shall have no power to veto any action of the Council.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.040)
§ 3.05.080  MAYOR PRO TEM OR TEMPORARY MAYOR.
   (A)   During a temporary absence or disability of the Mayor, the
Commissioner of Accounts and Finances shall serve as Temporary Mayor.
   (B)   Under circumstances in which the Mayor is or becomes disabled beyond a
temporary occurrence or otherwise incapable of performing his or her duties as
Mayor, the Commissioner of Accounts and Finances shall serve as Mayor Pro Tem.
   (C)   In the absence of both the Mayor and the Commissioner of Accounts and
Finances, the Commissioner of Public Property shall act in the capacity as
Temporary Mayor or Mayor Pro Tem, as the case may be.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.050)
COMMISSIONERS
§ 3.05.100  TERM.
   The Commissioners shall serve until their successors are elected and
qualified as provided by statute.
(Prior Code, § 2.12.010)
§ 3.05.105  COMMISSIONER OF PUBLIC AFFAIRS.
   (A)   The Mayor shall serve as the Commissioner of Public Affairs.
   (B)   As such, he or she shall control and manage the Police Department.
(Prior Code, § 2.12.020)
§ 3.05.110  COMMISSIONER OF ACCOUNTS AND FINANCES.
   The Commissioner of Accounts and Finances shall be the Superintendent of
Accounts and Finances and as such shall manage and control all of the financial
affairs of the village and report to the Council regarding the same.
(Prior Code, § 2.12.030)
§ 3.05.115  COMMISSIONER OF PUBLIC HEALTH AND SAFETY.
   The Commissioner of Public Health and Safety shall manage and control parks,
non-sewer drainage within the village and matters of public health and safety
and shall report to the Council regarding the same.
(Prior Code, § 2.12.040)
§ 3.05.120  COMMISSIONER OF PUBLIC PROPERTY.
   The Commissioner of Public Property shall manage and control the water and
sewer systems in the village and shall report to the Council regarding the
same.
(Prior Code, § 2.12.050)
§ 3.05.125  COMMISSIONER OF STREETS AND PUBLIC IMPROVEMENTS.
   The Commissioner of Streets and Public Improvements shall manage and control
the street system of the village and shall report to the Council regarding the
same.
(Prior Code, § 2.12.060)
§ 3.05.130  BOND.
   Each Commissioner shall execute and cause to be filed the appropriate bond
required in §§
3.05.005 through
3.05.045.
(Prior Code, § 2.12.070)
§ 3.05.135  SALARY.
   The Mayor and Commissioner shall each receive compensation as may be
determined by ordinance, except that neither the Mayor nor any of the Village
Commissioners shall receive an increase or decrease in compensation during
their respective terms of office. All compensation payable to either the Mayor
or the Village Commissioners shall be reviewed and approved consistent with
Illinois law.
(Prior Code, § 2.12.080)
VILLAGE COUNCIL
§ 3.05.150  REGULAR MEETINGS.
   Regular meetings of the Gardner Village Council shall be held on the first
Monday after the Mayor and Commissioners have entered upon the performance of
their official duties, and on the second and fourth Mondays of each month
thereafter, or as the Village Council may otherwise direct.
(Prior Code, § 2.16.010)
§ 3.05.155  SPECIAL MEETINGS.
   Special meetings of the Village Council may be called from time to time by
the Mayor, by two Commissioners or upon motion of the Village Council. Any
special meeting shall not occur unless notice of any special meeting is posted
not less than 48 hours prior to the date and time of any special meeting, and
an agenda of the special meeting shall also be posted within the 48-hour
period. Any special meeting shall also comply in all respects with the Illinois
Open Meetings Act, as amended.
(Prior Code, § 2.16.020)
§ 3.05.160  EMERGENCY MEETINGS.
   (A)   Emergency meetings of the Village Council may be called from time to
time by the Mayor or by any Commissioner, except that an emergency meeting of
the Gardner Village Council shall only be held in the event of a bona fide
emergency. Notice of an emergency meeting shall be given as soon as
practicable, but in any event prior to the holding of any emergency meeting.
Any notice of an emergency meeting shall also require the posting of an agenda
for the emergency meeting. Both the notice of emergency meeting and agenda
shall be posted at the Gardner Village Hall or at the building in which the
emergency meeting is to be held. The Gardner Village Council shall also supply
copies of the notice of any emergency meeting to any news media that has filed
an annual request for the notice.
   (B)   Any emergency meeting shall also comply in all respects with the
Illinois Open Meetings Act, as amended.
§ 3.05.165  POWERS AND DUTIES.
   The Village Council and its members shall possess and exercise all
executive, administrative and legislative powers and duties as may be provided
to executive, administrative and legislative officers under the state municipal
code, as amended.
(Prior Code, § 2.16.030)
§ 3.05.170  QUORUM; VOTING.
   Three members of the Village Council shall constitute a quorum, and the
affirmative vote of three members shall be necessary to adopt any motion,
resolution or ordinance, unless a greater number is required by statute.
(Prior Code, § 2.16.040)
§ 3.05.175  ORDER OF BUSINESS.
   The order of business at all regular meetings of the Village Council shall
be as follows:
   (A)   Roll call;
   (B)   Reading of the minutes of the previous meeting;
   (C)   Bills read and considered for approval;
   (D)   Communications;
   (E)   Old business;
   (F)   New business;
   (G)   Report from Attorney; and
   (H)   Reports of Commissioners.
(Prior Code, § 2.16.050)
§ 3.05.180  RECONSIDERATION OF PRIOR ACTION.
   (A)   A vote or question may be reconsidered at any time during the same
meeting or at the first regular meeting held thereafter. A motion for
reconsideration, once having been made and decided in the negative, shall not
be renewed, nor shall a motion to reconsider be reconsidered.
   (B)   No motion to reconsider the approval or denial of the recommendation
of an advisory body required to hold public hearings shall be entertained
except at the same meeting at which the original action was taken or after the
matter has subsequently been referred back to the advisory body for further
hearing and recommendation. When a motion to reconsider a motion is made at the
same meeting as the passage of the original motion, it may be tabled to a later
date certain.
   (C)   A motion to reconsider of a public body must be made by a member who
voted on the prevailing side of the question to be reconsidered, unless
otherwise provided by law; provided, however, that, when a motion has received
a majority vote in the affirmative, but is declared lost solely on the ground
that a greater number of affirmative votes are required by statute for the
passage or adoption of the motion, then a motion to reconsider may be made only
by those who vote in the affirmative on the question.
(Prior Code, § 2.16.060)
§ 3.05.185  ADDRESSING MEETINGS.
   No person other than the Mayor or a Commissioner shall address the Village
Council at a regular, special or emergency meeting, except upon the
authorization of either the Mayor, or upon motion and the consent of a majority
of the Commissioners present. The Mayor may limit the time available for public
comment.
(Prior Code, § 2.16.070)
Cross-reference:
   Citizen participation at public meetings, see §
3.20.035
§ 3.05.190  SUSPENSION OF RULES.
   The rules of order, other than those prescribed by statute, may be suspended
at any time by the consent of a majority of the members at any meeting.
(Prior Code, § 2.16.080)
§ 3.05.195  ROBERT’S RULES OF ORDER.
   Robert’s Rules of Order (latest edition) shall govern the deliberations of
the Village Council except when in conflict with any other rules set forth in
this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 2.16.090)
VILLAGE CLERK AND DEPUTY CLERK
§ 3.05.210  APPOINTIVE OFFICER.
   The Village Clerk shall be appointed by the Council as provided in §§
3.05.005 through
3.05.045.
(Prior Code, § 2.20.010)
§ 3.05.215  ATTENDANCE AT PUBLIC COUNCIL MEETINGS; RECORD-KEEPING.
   The Village Clerk shall attend all meetings of the corporate authorities
including executive sessions, and shall keep a full record of its proceedings
in a journal, except if the Clerk is the subject matter of the meeting and his
or her presence creates a conflict of interest.  In that event, the Village
Council reserves the right to determine whether any such conflict of interest
exists.
(Prior Code, § 2.20.020)
Statutory reference:
   Duties of Clerk; authority, see 65 ILCS 5/3.1-35-90
§ 3.05.220  ATTESTATION OF DOCUMENTS.
   The Village Clerk shall seal and attest all contracts of the village and all
licenses and other such documents as require this formality.
(Prior Code, § 2.20.030)
§ 3.05.225  DISPOSITION OF COLLECTED MONIES.
   The Clerk shall turn over all money received by him or her on behalf of the
village to the Village Treasurer, promptly on receipt of the same, and with the
money shall give a statement as to the source thereof.
(Prior Code, § 2.20.040)
§ 3.05.230  ACCOUNT KEEPING.
   The Clerk shall keep accounts showing all money received by him or her, and
the source and disposition thereof, and the other accounts as may be required
by statute or ordinance.
(Prior Code, § 2.20.050)
§ 3.05.235  RECORD-KEEPING.
   The Clerk shall have custody and control of all the municipal documents,
books and papers which he or she is required by statute or ordinance to keep.
(Prior Code, § 2.20.060)
§ 3.05.240  SEAL.
   The Clerk shall be the custodian of the village seal, and shall affix its
impression on documents whenever this is required.
(Prior Code, § 2.20.070)
§ 3.05.245  CUSTODIAN OF DOCUMENTS.
   The Clerk shall be the custodian of all documents belonging to the village
which are not assigned to the custody of some other officer of the village by
the Mayor or Council.
(Prior Code, § 2.20.080)
§ 3.05.250  INDEX MAINTENANCE.
   The Clerk shall keep and maintain a proper index to all documents and
records kept by him or her, so that ready access thereto and use thereof may be
had.
(Prior Code, § 2.20.090)
§ 3.05.255  PUBLICATION AUTHORITY.
   The Clerk shall cause to be published all ordinances, notices, reports and
other documents required to be published by statute.
(Prior Code, § 2.20.100)
§ 3.05.260  SUPERVISION OF REVENUE-RELATED EMPLOYEES.
   The Village Clerk shall have supervision over all officers and employees of
the village charged in any manner with the receipt, collection or disbursement
of village revenue, or with the collection and return of the village revenue
into the Treasury.
(Prior Code, § 2.20.110)
§ 3.05.265  WARRANT RECORD-KEEPING.
   The Village Clerk shall keep a record of all warrants or orders filed with
him or her or paid by him or her and all vouchers as is required by statute.
(Prior Code, § 2.20.120)
§ 3.05.270  ADDITIONAL DUTIES.
   The Village Clerk shall perform additional duties and have the additional
powers as the Council may by ordinance or resolution confer upon him or her.
(Prior Code, § 2.20.130)
§ 3.05.275  DEPUTY VILLAGE CLERK; OFFICE CREATED.
   There is created, as an officer of the village, the Office of Deputy Village
Clerk.
(Prior Code, § 2.20.140)
§ 3.05.280  DEPUTY VILLAGE CLERK; POWERS AND DUTIES.
   The Village Council may appoint one Deputy Clerk who shall have the power
and duty to execute all documents required by any law or ordinance to be
executed by the Clerk, and affix the seal of the village thereto whenever
required.
(Prior Code, § 2.20.150)
§ 3.05.285  DEPUTY VILLAGE CLERK; COMPENSATION.
   The salary of the Office of Deputy Village Clerk shall be as determined by
the Mayor and Village Council.
(Prior Code, § 2.20.160)
§ 3.05.290  VILLAGE CLERK TO HOLD OFFICE OF VILLAGE COLLECTOR.
   The Village Clerk shall hold the Office of the Village Collector.
(Prior Code, § 2.20.170)
§ 3.05.295  POWERS AND DUTIES OF VILLAGE COLLECTOR.
   The Village Collector shall have all the powers and duties as provided by
the statutes and laws of the state.
(Prior Code, § 2.20.180)
VILLAGE TREASURER
§ 3.05.310  APPOINTIVE OFFICER.
   The Village Treasurer shall be appointed by the Council as provided in §§
3.05.005 through
3.05.045.
(Prior Code, § 2.24.010)
§ 3.05.315  DUTIES GENERALLY.
   (A)   The Treasurer shall perform the duties as may be prescribed for him or
her by statute or by ordinance.
   (B)   He or she shall receive all money paid to the village, either directly
from the person paying it or from the hands of the other officer as may receive
it, and he or she shall pay out money only on vouchers or orders properly
signed by the City Clerk and the Mayor.
(Prior Code, § 2.24.020)
§ 3.05.320  DEPOSIT OF FUNDS.
   He or she shall deposit the village funds in the depositories as may be
selected from time to time as is provided by law, and he or she shall keep the
village money separate and distinct from his or her own and shall not
intermingle his or her own money with it or make private or personal use of the
village funds.
(Prior Code, § 2.24.030)
§ 3.05.325  RECORD-KEEPING.
   (A)   The Treasurer shall keep records showing all money received by him or
her, the source from which it was received, and the purpose for which it was
paid out.
   (B)   He or she shall keep a record showing at all times the financial
status of the village.
(Prior Code, § 2.24.040)
§ 3.05.330  ACCOUNT-KEEPING.
   The Treasurer shall keep the books and accounts as may be required by the
Village Council, and shall keep them in the manner required by the Village
Council.
(Prior Code, § 2.24.050)
§ 3.05.335  REPORTS.
   (A)   The Treasurer shall make monthly reports to the Council showing the
state of finances of the village, and the amount received and spent during the
month, which reports shall be filed.
   (B)   He or she shall make an annual report after the close of the fiscal
year, as required by statute with the total amount of all receipts and
expenditures of the village and his or her transactions as treasurer during the
preceding year.
(Prior Code, § 2.24.060)
VILLAGE ATTORNEY
§ 3.05.350  APPOINTIVE OFFICE.
   The Village Attorney shall be appointed by the Council as provided in §§
3.05.005 through
3.05.045.
(Prior Code, § 2.28.010)
§ 3.05.355  SUPERVISION OF DRAFTING OF ORDINANCES AND DOCUMENTS.
   The Attorney shall, on direction of the Mayor or Village Council, draft or
supervise the drafting of all ordinances and resolutions to be acted on, and
all contracts or other documents in which the village is interested.
(Prior Code, § 2.28.020)
§ 3.05.360  RESPONSIBILITY FOR SUITS AND ACTIONS OF VILLAGE.
   The Attorney shall prosecute or defend any and all suits or actions at law
or equity to which the village may be a party or in which it may be interested,
or which may be brought against or by any officer of the village on behalf of
the village or in the capacity of the person as an officer of the village.
(Prior Code, § 2.28.030)
§ 3.05.365  LEGAL ADVISOR FOR VILLAGE.
   The Attorney shall be the legal advisor of the village and shall render
advice on all legal questions affecting it.
(Prior Code, § 2.28.040)
§ 3.05.370  ATTENDANCE AT COUNCIL MEETINGS.
   The Attorney shall attend all meetings of the Village Council.
(Prior Code, § 2.28.050)
§ 3.05.375  COMPENSATION.
   (A)   The Attorney shall receive the compensation as may be decided from
time to time by the Village Council as an annual salary for attending Council
meetings and giving advice.
   (B)   He or she shall receive additional compensation as agreed by the
Council from time to time for other work on behalf of the village.
(Prior Code, § 2.28.060)
BUILDING INSPECTOR
§ 3.05.390  CREATED; APPOINTMENT.
   There is created the position of Building Inspector, who shall be appointed
by the Council.
(Prior Code, § 2.32.010)
§ 3.05.395  DUTIES.
   It shall be the duty of the Building Inspector to see to the enforcement of
all ordinance provisions relating to buildings or zoning and to inspect all
buildings or structures being erected or altered, as frequently as may be
necessary to insure compliance with the ordinances of the village.
(Prior Code, § 2.32.020)
§ 3.05.400  STOP ORDER.
   (A)   The Building Inspector shall have the power to order all work stopped
on construction or alteration or repair of buildings in the village when the
work is being done in violation of any provision of any ordinance relating
thereto, or in violation of any zoning ordinance.
   (B)   Work shall not be resumed after the issuance of such an order, except
on the written permission of the Inspector; provided, that if the stop order is
an oral one, it shall be followed by an written stop order within 24 hours.
   (C)   The written stop order may be served by any Village Inspector, the
Mayor, any Commissioner or any Police Officer, except that any the stop work
order shall not be removed by any person other than the person who issued the
stop work order.
(Prior Code, § 2.32.030)
§ 3.05.405  RIGHT OF ENTRY FOR INSPECTION.
   The Building Inspector shall have the power to make or cause to be made an
entry into any building or premises where the work of altering, repairing or
constructing is going on, for the purpose of making inspection, at any
reasonable hour.
(Prior Code, § 2.32.040)
BOARD OF LOCAL IMPROVEMENTS
§ 3.05.420  ESTABLISHED.
   There is established a Board of Local Improvements which shall consist of
the Mayor, the Commissioner of Streets and Public Improvements and the
Commissioner of Accounts and Finances.
(Prior Code, § 2.36.010)
§ 3.05.425  POWERS AND DUTIES.
   (A)   The Board of Local Improvements shall meet at the times and places as
may be designated by the Board and shall have the powers and duties assigned to
it by statute or ordinance.
   (B)   Every improvement to be paid for by special assessments or special
taxation shall be initiated by the action of the Board of Local Improvements as
required by law.
(Prior Code, § 2.36.020)
LIQUOR COMMISSIONER
§ 3.05.440  MAYOR TO SERVE.
   The Mayor of the village shall serve as the Liquor Commissioner of the
village without any remuneration for the service other than that provided as
salary of the Mayor by ordinance, as required by law.
(Prior Code, § 2.40.010)
POLICE DEPARTMENT
§ 3.05.455  POLICE DEPARTMENT CREATED; MEMBERS; CONTRACTUAL LAW ENFORCEMENT
SERVICES.
   There is hereby created a Police Department, an executive department of the
village. The Police Department shall consist of the Chief of Police and of the
number of Captains, Lieutenants, Sergeants and Patrol Officers as may be
provided from time to time by the Village Council. In the absence of a Village
Police Department, the Gardner Village Council is expressly authorized to
contract with the County of Grundy and/or the Grundy County Sheriff’s
Department for contractual police services throughout the Village of Gardner as
the Gardner Village Council may deem reasonable or appropriate and to authorize
and approve the expenditures of sums as the Gardner Village Council may
determine.
(Prior Code, § 2.52.010)
§ 3.05.460  POLICE CHIEF; OFFICE CREATED.
   There is created the Office of the Chief of Police. The Chief shall be
appointed by the Mayor with the consent of the Village Council. He or she shall
be ex-officio City Marshal and Superintendent of Police.
(Prior Code, § 2.52.020)
§ 3.05.465  POLICE CHIEF; DUTIES.
   The Chief of Police shall be the keeper of the village jail and shall have
custody of all persons incarcerated therein. He or she shall keep the records
and make the reports concerning the activities of this Department as may be
required by statute or by the Village Council.
(Prior Code, § 2.52.030)
§ 3.05.470  POLICE CHIEF; ADDITIONAL DUTIES.
   The Chief of Police shall be ex-officio pound master and perform the duties
connected with the care and maintenance of the pound and the animals
incarcerated therein.
(Prior Code, § 2.52.040)
§ 3.05.475  DUTIES OF MEMBERS.
   It shall be the duty of the members of the Police Department to see to the
enforcement of all ordinances of the village, of all statutes effective in the
village, and to preserve the order and prevent infractions of the law and to
arrest violators thereof.
(Prior Code, § 2.52.050)
§ 3.05.480  INTERFERENCE WITH POLICE OFFICERS.
   Any person in the village who resists any member of the Police Department or
any other person duly authorized to perform police duty in the discharge of his
or her duties or in any way interferes with, prevents or hinders him or her in
the discharge of his or her duty as the member, or offers or endeavors to do
so, and any person who in any manner assists any person in the custody of any
member of the Police Department to escape or attempt to escape from the custody
shall be punished by a fine not exceeding $750.
(Prior Code, § 2.52.060)
§ 3.05.485  DUTY OF CITIZENS TO ASSIST POLICE.
   It shall be the duty of every citizen in the village, when called upon by a
member of the Police Department and in case of an emergency, to promptly aid
and assist the officer(s) in the execution of his or her police duties. Any
person who refuses to give aid and assistance shall be punished by a fine not
less than $75 nor more than $750.
(Prior Code, § 2.52.070)
§ 3.05.490  CONDUCT OF MEMBERS.
   It shall be the duty of every member of the Police Department to conduct
himself or herself in a proper and law-abiding manner.
(Prior Code, § 2.52.080)
§ 3.05.495  POWER TO SERVE LEGAL PAPERS.
   The Chief of Police and all patrol officers shall have the power and
authority to serve writs, summons, warrants and other legal papers for the
apprehension and commitment of persons charged with violation of any village
ordinance, or charged with the commission of any crime, or misdemeanor, or
offense against the laws of the village or state, or held for examination or
trial.
(Prior Code, § 2.52.090)
§ 3.05.500  CUSTODY OF STOLEN PROPERTY.
   The Chief of Police shall have the custody of all lost, abandoned or stolen
property recovered in the village.
(Prior Code, § 2.52.110)
OFFICE OF FIRE INSPECTOR
§ 3.05.520  CREATED; APPOINTMENT.
   There is created the position of Fire Inspector, who shall be appointed by
and serve at the pleasure of the Council.
(Ord. G-127, passed 3-23-1992)
§ 3.05.525  DUTIES.
   It shall be the duty of the Fire Inspector to inspect for hazardous fire
conditions existing on any property located in the village.
(Ord. G-127, passed 3-23-1992)
§ 3.05.999  PENALTY.
   Any firm, person or corporation who continues work in violation of a stop
order of the Zoning and Building Officer shall be fined not less than $75 nor
more than $750 for each day on which any work in violation of the order is
done.
(Prior Code, § 2.32.050)

APPROPRIATIONS AND EXPENDITURES
§ 3.10.005  APPROPRIATION ORDINANCE TO BE ENACTED.
   (A)   During the first quarter of each fiscal year, as required by statute,
the Mayor and Village Council shall adopt an appropriation ordinance in which
shall be itemized all anticipated expenditures to be met during the coming
year, other than those payable from bond issues. The appropriation ordinance
shall appropriate sums of money as the municipality deems necessary to defray
all its necessary expenses and liabilities, specifically including the amounts
required to be deposited and reserves established for pension purposes.
   (B)   At the time the Gardner Village Council adopts an appropriation
ordinance, the Village Council shall also prepare and adopt an accounting of
the village's estimated revenues by source that the municipality anticipates
receiving during the same fiscal year covered by the appropriation ordinance.
The estimated revenues by source must also identify the source of all revenues
on a line item basis. The estimated revenues by source must be certified by the
Village Treasurer.
   (C)   Within 30 days after the adoption of its appropriation ordinance and
estimated revenues by source as set forth above, the Village Clerk shall file a
certified copy of the ordinance and estimated revenues by source with the
County Clerk.  The Village Clerk shall also publish a true and correct copy of
the appropriation ordinance and the estimated revenues by source following the
adoption thereof pursuant to Illinois law.
(Prior Code, § 3.04.010)
§ 3.10.010  TAX LEVY ORDINANCE.
   (A)   No sooner than ten days after the publication of the appropriation
ordinance, a tax levy ordinance shall be enacted, as required by law, levying
the taxes as may be needed to meet the anticipated expenses of the coming year,
together with taxes as may be required to meet outstanding bond issues, or for
purposes payable from special taxes properly authorized.
   (B)   A certified copy of the tax levy ordinance shall be filed with the
County Clerk not later than the last Tuesday in December as is provided by
statute. The tax levy ordinance shall show the amounts appropriated for each
line item and the amount of tax levied therefore.
(Prior Code, § 3.04.020)
§ 3.10.015  CONTRACT; EXPENDITURES; APPROPRIATIONS.
   (A)   No contract shall be made by the village or by any committee or member
thereof, and no expense shall be incurred by any of the officers or departments
of the village, whether the object of the expenditure has been ordered by the
village or not, unless an appropriation has been previously made concerning
that contract or expense.
   (B)   Any contract made, or any expense otherwise incurred, in violation of
the provisions of this section shall be null and void as to the village, and no
money belonging thereto shall be paid on account thereof.
   (C)   However, pending the passage of the annual appropriation ordinance for
any fiscal year, the village may authorize heads of department to make
necessary expenditures for the support thereof upon the basis of the
appropriation of the preceding fiscal year.
   (D)   However, if it is determined by two-thirds vote of the Council members
then holding office at a regularly scheduled meeting of the Council that it is
expedient and in the best public interests to begin proceedings for the
construction of a needed public work, then the provisions of this section shall
not apply to the extent that the Council may employ or contract for
professional services necessary for the planning and financing of the public
works.
(Prior Code, § 3.04.030)
§ 3.10.020  AUDIT REQUIRED.
   (A)   (1)   As soon as practicable at the close of each fiscal year, and no
later than six months thereafter, the Village Council shall cause an audit of
all accounts of the village to be made by a competent person authorized to act
as an independent auditor under the laws of the state, to be designated by the
Mayor and approved by the Village Council.
      (2)   The person performing the audit shall possess valid credentials as
a certified public accountant.
   (B)   Copies of the audit report shall be filed with the Village Clerk and
with the Director of the State Department of Revenue and in other places as may
be required by law.
(Prior Code, § 3.04.040)
MUNICIPAL RETAILER’S OCCUPATION TAX
§ 3.10.035  IMPOSITION.
   A tax is imposed upon all persons engaged in the business of selling
tangible personal property at retail in this village at the rate of 1% of the
gross receipts from the sales made in the course of the business while this
chapter is in effect, in accordance with the provisions of 65 ILCS 5/8-11-1.
(Prior Code, § 3.08.010)
§ 3.10.040  REPORT TO BE FILED.
   Every person engaged in business in the village shall file on or before the
last day of each calendar month the report to the State Department of Revenue
required by § 3 of “An Act in Relation to a Tax upon Persons Engaged in the
Business of Selling Tangible Personal Property to Purchasers for Use or
Consumption” approved June 28, 1933, as amended.
(Prior Code, § 3.08.020)
§ 3.10.045  PAYMENT.
   At the time the report is filed, there shall be paid to the State Department
of Revenue the amount of tax imposed in §
3.10.035 on account of the preceding month.
(Prior Code, § 3.08.030)
MUNICIPAL SERVICE OCCUPATION TAX
§ 3.10.060  IMPOSITION.
   A tax is imposed in accordance with the provisions of § 8-11-5 of the
Illinois Municipal Code upon the business of making sales of service at the
rate not to exceed 1% of the cost price of all tangible personal property
transferred by the service persons in the form of tangible personal property or
in the form of real estate as an incident to a sale of service.
(Prior Code, § 3.12.010)
§ 3.10.065  COLLECTION.
   The tax shall be collected by the State Department of Revenue for all
municipalities imposing the tax and shall be paid before the title or
certificate of registration for personal property is issued, if any.
(Prior Code, § 3.12.020)

CHAPTER 3.20: SPECIFIC POLICIES AND PROCEDURES
Section
   
3.20.005   Ethics Act
