9.20.999   Penalty
ABANDONED REFRIGERATORS
§ 9.20.005  UNLAWFUL.
   It is unlawful for any person to abandon or discard in any place accessible
to children any refrigerator, icebox or ice chest, of a capacity of one and
one-half cubic feet or more which has an attached lid or door which may be
opened or fastened shut by means of an attached latch, or for the manager,
owner or lessee of the premises to knowingly permit the refrigerator, ice chest
or icebox to remain in such condition.
(Prior Code, § 8.04.010)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
BONFIRES
§ 9.20.015  UNLAWFUL WHEN.
   It is unlawful to build or light any bonfire so close to any building or
other structure as to endanger the building or structure.
(Prior Code, § 8.08.010)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
CONTAGIOUS DISEASES
§ 9.20.030  REPORT REQUIRED.
   Every physician called in to care for or treat a person afflicted with a
contagious disease or an epidemic disease shall make a report of the same
within 24 hours after being called in, to the Health Officer. In case no
physician is in attendance, it shall be the duty of the person in charge of or
having the care of the person to make a report within 24 hours from the time
the disease is recognized.
(Prior Code, § 8.12.010)
§ 9.20.035  QUARANTINE.
   The Commissioner of Public Safety shall have charge of the enforcement of
the reasonable quarantine rules. He or she shall have the power and the
authority to place any premises within which a contagious or epidemic disease
occurs under quarantine, and shall determine the time when the quarantine ends.
(Prior Code, § 8.12.020)
§ 9.20.040  FUMIGATION.
   Premises which have been quarantined in accordance with the terms of §
9.20.035 shall be thoroughly fumigated or otherwise freed from all risk of
contagious disease under the supervision of the Commissioner of Public Safety
before the quarantine shall end.
(Prior Code, § 8.12.030)
§ 9.20.045  SPREADING CONTAGION UNLAWFUL.
   It is unlawful for any person to spread, wilfully or carelessly, any
contagious disease or to so cause the spread of the same.
(Prior Code, § 8.12.040)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
§ 9.20.050  DELIVERIES TO QUARANTINE PREMISES.
   No person engaged in the delivery of food or drink intended for human
consumption shall enter any premises which are quarantined because of the
existence of a contagious or epidemic disease. No containers or bottles shall
be removed from any premises until the termination of the quarantine, and no
container which has been left at the premises during the quarantine shall be
placed in use for carrying food or drink until it has been thoroughly
sterilized.
(Prior Code, § 8.12.050)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
EXPLOSIVES
§ 9.20.070  POSSESSION OF EXPLOSIVES.
   No person shall possess, manufacture, use, transport or store explosives, as
defined in 225 ILCS 210/1003, in the village unless he or she holds a current
license for the same issued by the Department of Mines and Minerals of the
state, and unless the same is in compliance with the statutes of the state and
the rules and regulations promulgated by the Department of Mines and Minerals.
(Prior Code, § 8.16.010)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
FIREWORKS
§ 9.20.085  DEFINED.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   FIREWORKS.
      (1)   Any explosive composition, or any substance or combination of
substances, or article prepared for the purpose of producing a visible or
audible effect of a temporary exhibitional nature by explosion, combustion,
deflagration or detonation, and shall include blank cartridges, toy cannons, in
which explosives are used, the type of balloons which require fire underneath
to propel the same, firecrackers, torpedoes, skyrockets, Roman candles, bombs
or other fireworks of like construction and any fireworks containing any
explosive compounds, or any tablets or other device containing any explosive
substance, or containing combustible substances producing visual effects.
      (2)   The term FIREWORKS shall not include snake or glow worm pellets;
smoke devices; sparklers; trick noisemakers known as “party poppers,” “booby
traps,” “snappers,” “trick matches,” “cigarette loads,” and “auto burglar
alarms”; toy pistols, toy canes, toy guns or other devices in which paper or
plastic caps containing 25/100 grains or less of explosive compound are used,
provided they are so constructed that the hand cannot come in contact with the
cap when in place for the explosion, and toy pistol paper or plastic caps which
contain less than 25/100 grains of explosive mixture, the sale and use of which
shall be permitted at all times.
(Prior Code, § 8.20.010)
§ 9.20.090  PERMIT REQUIRED.
   No person shall store or discharge any fireworks, as defined in §
9.20.085, without a permit issued by the Village Council upon application as
provided in §
9.20.095.
(Prior Code, § 8.20.020)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
§ 9.20.095  PERMIT APPLICATION.
   (A)   Any group of three or more adult individuals or any corporation may
apply to the Village Council in writing for a permit to store and discharge
fireworks within the village limits.
   (B)   The application shall be made at a Council meeting 15 days proceeding
the date of the proposed event.
   (C)   It shall also include the name of the individual proposed to operate
the display, who must be approved by the Council, and a bond in the amount of
$1,000 conditioned upon compliance with the state law regarding fireworks
displays and with the rules and regulations of the State Fire Marshal regarding
the same.
   (D)   The Council shall cause the proposed site of the display to be
inspected to determine that the display will not be hazardous to property or
endanger any person or persons, and shall grant or deny the permit within 48
hours of the application therefore.
   (E)   The Village Clerk shall cause one copy of each application and permit
to be filed at the office of the State Fire Marshal.
(Prior Code, § 8.20.030)
§ 9.20.100  COMPLIANCE REQUIRED.
   No person or corporation shall store or discharge fireworks in a manner as
to be hazardous to property or endanger any person or persons or in a manner
not otherwise in compliance with the rules and regulations of the State Fire
Marshal regarding the same.
(Prior Code, § 8.20.040)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
FLAMMABLE LIQUID STORAGE
§ 9.20.115  STORAGE REGULATIONS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to store any crude petroleum, benzine,
gasoline, naphtha or other combustible liquid in the village except in a manner
consistent with the regulations regarding the storage promulgated by the State
Fire Marshal.
(Prior Code, § 8.24.010)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
FOOD DEALERS; GENERALLY
§ 9.20.130  DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context indicates or requires a different meaning.
   FOOD.  Includes beverages.
   FOOD DEALER.  Includes every person, firm or corporation engaged in,
conducting, or operating any of the following businesses:
      (1)   Bakeries, or any establishment for the mixing, compounding or
baking for sale, or purpose of a restaurant, any bread or breadstuffs or any
food product of which flour or meal is the principal ingredient; provided, that
places where the foodstuffs are baked in restaurant kitchens for consumption in
the restaurant only, or in dwellings where the foodstuffs are baked on ordinary
ranges or stoves for consumption on the premises only, shall not be considered
as bakeries;
      (2)   Fruit store or establishment for the retail sale of fresh fruit and
berries;
      (3)   Grocery store, or establishment for the sale at retail of butter,
cheese, vegetables or other provisions;
      (4)   Ice cream parlor; and
      (5)   Meat market, or establishment for the retail sale of fresh meat,
poultry and fish.
(Prior Code, § 8.28.010)
§ 9.20.135  SALE OF UNWHOLESOME FOOD; UNLAWFUL.
   No person, firm or corporation shall offer for sale, or keep for the purpose
of selling, or offering for sale, any food of any kind intended for human
consumption which is soiled or tainted or is unwholesome and unfit for human
consumption for any reason.
(Prior Code, § 8.28.020)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
§ 9.20.140  ADULTERATION OF FOOD; UNLAWFUL.
   It is unlawful to sell, offer for sale, or keep for the purpose any food or
drink intended for human consumption which has been adulterated by any material
harmful in any way or which does not comply with the statutes governing the
same.
(Prior Code, § 8.28.030)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
§ 9.20.145  SANITARY REGULATIONS.
   No person, firm or corporation shall operate a business as a food dealer
unless he or she is in compliance with all rules and regulations promulgated by
the State Department of Public Health and the County Health Department.
(Prior Code, § 8.28.040)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
RESTAURANTS
§ 9.20.160  DEFINITIONS.
   As used in this subchapter, RESTAURANT includes any place where food or
drink (other than alcoholic liquor) is prepared or served to the public for
consumption on the premises. FOOD includes beverages other than alcoholic
liquor.
(Prior Code, § 8.32.010)
§ 9.20.165  SANITARY REGULATIONS.
   No person, firm or corporation shall operate a restaurant within the village
limits which is not in compliance with the rules and regulations regarding the
same promulgated by the State Department of Public Health and the County Health
Department.
(Prior Code, § 8.32.020)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
GARBAGE AND REFUSE COLLECTION
§ 9.20.180  DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ASHES.  Residue from fires used for cooking and for heating buildings.
   GARBAGE.  The general accumulations of animal, fruit or vegetable matter
that attend the preparation, use cooking, dealing in or storage of meat, fish
fowl, fruits or vegetables and containers originally used for foodstuffs.
   REFUSE.  The general accumulations of waste materials as may be accumulated
day to day in an average residential unit including:
      (1)   Papers, cartons, boxes, furniture, box springs, mattresses, bath
tubs and discarded appliances; and
      (2)   But shall not include such items as: broken concrete, building
materials, rocks, fallen trees, dirt or any household item too large to be
placed in a compactor-type truck.
   RUBBISH.  Garbage, refuse or both.
   YARDWASTE.  (Trees, shrubs, grass clippings and leaves) are not considered
rubbish.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.36)  (Ord. G-115, passed 5-27-1986; Ord. G-128, passed
6-2-1992)
§ 9.20.185  GARBAGE TO BE DEPOSITED IN CONTAINERS.
   (A)   All garbage created, accumulated or produced shall be deposited in
containers of a type approved by the Commissioner of Public Health and Safety
of the village, equipped with suitable handles and tight fitting covers, and
shall be water-tight.
   (B)   Each container shall have a capacity of not less than five gallons and
not more than 30 gallons, and shall be kept in a clean, neat and sanitary
condition at all times.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.36)  (Ord. G-115, passed 5-27-1986)
§ 9.20.190  HOUSEHOLDER TO PROVIDE CONTAINERS.
   (A)   It shall be the duty of every person in possession, charge or control
of any place in or from which garbage is created, accumulated or produced, to
provide, and at all times keep in a suitable place readily accessible to the
garbage collector, not more than three garbage containers capable of holding
all garbage which would ordinarily accumulate on the premises between the time
of successive collections.
   (B)   (1)   The owner of any multiple dwelling shall furnish or require his
or her tenants to furnish proper garbage containers.
      (2)   Garbage containers located at multiple dwellings, if furnished by
the tenants, shall be marked so as to indicate the apartment or flat to which
they belong.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.36)  (Ord. G-115, passed 5-27-1986)
§ 9.20.195  MATERIALS DEPOSITED IN GARBAGE CONTAINERS.
   Garbage, refuse and ashes may be deposited in garbage containers. Human
waste and other potentially infectious material shall not be deposited or
placed in garbage containers unless the material is wrapped in a manner
satisfactory to the Commissioner of Public Health and Safety. Liquid garbage
shall not be deposited in the containers except in a sealed container. Kitchen
garbage shall be drained of all moisture and completely wrapped in paper or
plastic before it is placed or deposited in garbage containers.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.36)  (Ord. G-115, passed 5-27-1986)
§ 9.20.200  LOCATION OF CONTAINERS.
   No garbage containers or other containers for refuse, other than those of
the village, shall be placed, kept, stored or located within the right-of-way
of a street or alley.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.36)  (Ord. G-115, passed 5-27-1986)
§ 9.20.205  COLLECTION OF FEES; USE OF COLLECTION SERVICE REQUIRED.
   (A)   It is found that the periodic collection of garbage and refuse from
all residences in the village benefits all occupants in the village, and to the
extent that tax revenues are not sufficient to pay for the cost of the same,
the occupants or persons in possession, charge or control of any residence in
or from which garbage is created, accumulated or produced that is collected by
the village or its contractors are liable for and shall pay the garbage
collection fees established by the Village Council.
   (B)   Garbage collection service is provided by the village, and it shall be
mandatory for all occupants or persons in possession, charge or control of
places and premises in the village in or from which garbage is created,
accumulated or produced to use the village’s collection service.
   (C)   It shall be unlawful for any person other than authorized agents or
employees of the village to collect, remove or dispose of garbage at a
residence in the village; provided, however, that nothing contained in this
chapter shall prevent the use of garbage disposal devices as provided in the
village Plumbing Code. Provided further, any commercial establishment within
the Village of Gardner, which generates garbage or refuse as defined herein may
contract with a private scavenger service other than that which is employed by
the village for the removal of the same. In the event that the persons contract
with the scavenger employed by the village for the collection of garbage and
refuse at their commercial establishment, the village may contract with the
scavenger to provide a credit equal to the commercial establishment’s pro rata
share of the authorized real estate tax levy (garbage tax) to be applied
against monies owed the scavenger.
   (D)   The Village Council may enter into the contracts as are authorized by
Division 19 of the Illinois Municipal Code, as amended from time to time, (65
ILCS 5/11-19-1 et seq.) as are necessary to effectuate the efficient collection
and disposal of garbage, refuse and ashes as defined herein.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.36)  (Ord. G-115, passed 5-27-1986)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
§ 9.20.210  TIME FOR COLLECTION.
   Collection of garbage and refuse shall be made at least once a week from
residences or as many times per week as the Commissioner of Public Health and
Safety of the village may order.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.36)  (Ord. G-115, passed 5-27-1986)
§ 9.20.215  NOTIFICATION FOR COLLECTION.
   All occupants, persons in possession, charge or control of premises and
places in or upon which garbage or refuse is created, accumulated or produced
shall notify the Commissioner of Public Health and Safety of the village that
collection of garbage from the place is required.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.36)  (Ord. G-115, passed 5-27-1986)
§ 9.20.220  FEES.
   (A)   The fees assessed for collection of garbage, refuse and ashes in
addition to any authorized real estate tax levy (garbage tax) shall be assessed
only from persons receiving collection services. The Village Council may from
time to time by ordinance, establish a schedule of fees for collection services
and a copy of the schedule shall be furnished each customer.
   (B)   (1)   Payment of the fees referred to in division (A) above shall be
monthly, in advance.
      (2)   The Village Clerk may include a notice of current customers charges
with the then current water and sewer bill.
      (3)   Payment for all fees referred to herein shall be delinquent 30 days
after the bill for the fees has been mailed.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.36)  (Ord. G-115, passed 5-27-1986)
§ 9.20.225  BURNING PROHIBITED.
   (A)   No person shall burn garbage or refuse within the village limits.
   (B)   Nothing herein contained shall prohibit any person from burning
landscape waste, as defined by the Environmental Protection Act (415 ILCS 5/
3.270), generated from one’s own property.
   (C)   An individual burning landscape waste pursuant to division (B) shall
burn between the hours of 7:00 A.M. and 6:00 P.M.  Burning shall not be allowed
within two feet of any street, sidewalk, or alleyway (both improved and
unimproved).
   (D)   In addition to the penalties described in §
9.20.999, any individual who violates the provisions of this section shall be
responsible for the cost of repair to the village property.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.36)  (Ord. G-115, passed 5-27-1986; Ord. G 123, passed
10-8-1990; Ord. 001-2012, passed 1-9-2012)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
§ 9.20.230  NUISANCE.
   The keeping of garbage or refuse in containers other than containers
prescribed by this subchapter or the keeping upon premises of garbage or refuse
which is allowed to become offensive and noisome, shall constitute a public
nuisance and may be abated in the manner provided by law for the abatement of
nuisances.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.36)  (Ord. G-115, passed 5-27-1986)
§ 9.20.235  STORING AND COLLECTION.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful and deemed a public nuisance for garbage to be
placed on the street for collection in other than suitable containers as
required above any sooner than 4:00 p.m. the day before scheduled pick-up.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful and deemed a public nuisance to place the refuse
containers at the street for collection sooner than 4:00 p.m. the day before
scheduled pick-up.
   (C)   It shall be unlawful and deemed a public nuisance to leave refuse and
empty refuse containers at the pick-up site after 12:00 p.m. the day following
the day of scheduled pick-up.
(Ord. G98-163, passed 10-26-1998)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
§ 9.20.240  SCAVENGING OF RECYCLABLE MATERIALS FROM CURBSIDE RECYCLING BINS;
PROHIBITED.
   (A)   All “recyclables” as defined in any agreement between the Village of
Gardner and a scavenger service such as tin and aluminum cans, clear glass,
brown glass, green jars and bottles, chip board, newsprint and #1 and #2
plastic shall become the property of the scavenger service upon the placement
of the items upon the curb side for disposal.
   (B)   (1)   It shall be a violation of this section for any person or firm
or entity of any kind unauthorized by the householder or scavenger service to
collect or cause to be collected any of the “recyclable” items named in this
section from the curbside bins.
      (2)   Any and each collection in violation of this section shall
constitute a separate and distinct offense punishable as provided in this
section.
(Ord. G-135, passed 4-10-1995)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
NUISANCES
§ 9.20.260  DANGEROUS STRUCTURES PROHIBITED.
   It is unlawful to permit any building, structure or place to remain in such
a condition as to be dangerous to the public health in any way. Any structure,
building or place is a nuisance.
(Prior Code, § 8.40.010)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
§ 9.20.265  ENDANGERING ACTS PROHIBITED.
   It is unlawful to commit or do any act which endangers the public health.
(Prior Code, § 8.40.020)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
§ 9.20.270  NUISANCE ABATEMENT.
   It is unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to permit to maintain the
existence of any nuisance on any property under his, her or its control. The
Superintendent of Police and the Health Officer are each authorized to abate
any nuisances existing in the village, whether the nuisance is one specifically
recognized by ordinance or not.
(Prior Code, § 8.40.030)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
§ 9.20.275  PROHIBITING CERTAIN NUISANCES.
   (A)   Loud noise.  It shall be unlawful for any person to make, continue or
cause to be made or continued any excessive, unnecessary or unusually loud
noise or any noise which either annoys, disturbs, injures or endangers the
comfort, repose, health, peace or safety of others, within the limits of the
village.
   (B)   Noises prohibited; unnecessary noise standard.  The following acts,
among others, are declared to be loud, disturbing and unnecessary noises in
violation of this section, but the enumeration shall not be deemed to be
exclusive, namely:
      (1)   Horns, signaling devices and the like. The sounding of any horn or
signaling device on any automobile, motorcycle, streetcar or other vehicle on
any street or public place of the city, except as a danger warning; the
creation by means of any unreasonably loud or harsh sound; and the sounding of
any signaling devise of any device for an unnecessary and unreasonable period
of time. The use of any signaling device except one operated by hand or
electricity; the use of any horn, whistle or other device operated by engine
exhaust; and the use of any signaling device when traffic is for any reason
held up;
      (2)   Radios, phonographs and the like.  The using, operating or
permitting to be played, used or operated  any radio or television receiving
set, musical instrument, phonograph or other, machine or device for the
producing or reproducing of sound in such manner as to disturb the peace, quiet
and comfort of the neighboring inhabitants or at any time with louder volume
than is necessary for convenient hearing for the person or persons who are in
the room, vehicle or changer in which the machine or device is operated and who
are voluntary listeners thereto. The operation of any set, instrument,
phonograph, machine or device between the hours of 11:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m. in
such a manner as to be plainly audible at a distance of 50 feet from the
building, structure or vehicle in which it is located shall be prima facie
evidence of a violation of this section;
      (3)   Loud speakers, amplifiers for advertising.  The using, operating or
permitting to be played, used or operated of any radio receiving set, musical
instrument, phonograph, loudspeaker, sound amplifier or other machine or device
for the producing or reproducing of sound which is case upon the public streets
for the purpose of commercial advertising or attracting the attention of the
public to any building or structure;
      (4)   Yelling, shouting and the like.  Yelling, shouting, hooting,
whistling or singing on the public streets, particularly between the hours of
11:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m. or at any time or place so as to annoy or disturb the
quiet, comfort or repose of persons in any office, or in any dwelling, hotel or
other type of residence, or of any person in the vicinity;
      (5)   Animals, birds and the like.  The keeping of any animal or bird
which by causing frequent or long continued noise shall disturb the comfort or
repose of any persons in the vicinity;
      (6)   Exhausts.  The discharge into the open air of the exhaust of any
steam engine, stationary internal combustion engine, motor boat or motor
vehicle except through a muffler or device which will effectively prevent loud
or explosive noises therefrom;
      (7)   Loading, unloading, opening boxes. The creation of a loud and
excessive noise in connection with loading or unloading any vehicle or the
opening and destruction of bales, boxes, crates and containers;
      (8)   Construction or repairing of buildings. The erection (including
excavation), demolition, alteration or repair of the exterior of any building
other than between the hours of 7:30 a.m. and sunset except upon special permit
issued by the Building Commissioner or the Mayor, made upon their determination
that the public health and safety will not be impaired by the construction
activities. The prohibition contained in this section shall not apply to minor
erection, demolition, alteration or repair which work can be completed within a
period of one hour or which does not involve the operation of any mechanized
equipment or machinery;
      (9)   Schools, churches, hospitals.  The creation of any excessive noise
on any street adjacent to any school, institution of learning or church while
the same are in use, or adjacent to any hospital, which unreasonably interferes
with the workings of the institution, or which disturbs or unduly annoys
patients in the hospital, provided conspicuous signs are displaced in such
streets indicating that the same is a school or hospital street;
      (10)   Pile drivers, hammers and the like. The operation between the
hours of 10:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m. of any pile driver, steam shovel, pneumatic
hammer, derricks, steam or electric hoist, or other appliance, the use of which
is attended by loud or unusual noise; and
      (11)   Blowers. The operation of any noise-creating blower or power fan
or any internal combustion engine, the operation of which causes noise due to
the explosion of operating gases or fluids, unless the noise from the blower or
fan is muffled and the engine is equipped with a muffler device sufficient to
deaden the noise.
(Ord. G-122, passed 3-12-1989)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
PLANTS AND WEEDS
§ 9.20.290  WEEDS DEEMED NUISANCES.
   Any weeds such as marijuana, jimson, burdock, ragweed, thistle, cocklebur or
other weeds of a like kind found growing in any lot or tract of land in the
village are a nuisance, and it is unlawful to permit any such weeds to grow or
remain in any such place.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.44)  (Ord. VG06-407, passed 6-22-2006)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
§ 9.20.295  HEIGHT LIMIT.
   It is unlawful for anyone to permit weeds, grass or plants other than trees,
corn, beans or other agricultural products, bushes, flowers or other ornamental
plants to grow to a height exceeding six inches anywhere in the village. Any
such plants exceeding that height are a nuisance.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.44)  (Ord. VG06-407, passed 6-22-2006)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
§ 9.20.300  BARBERRY BUSHES.
   It is a nuisance and unlawful to plant or permit the growth of a bush of the
species of tall, common or European barberry, further known as Barberis
vulgaris, or its horticultural varieties within the village.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.44)  (Ord. VG06-407, passed 6-22-2006)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
§ 9.20.305  REMOVAL; NOTICE.
   It shall be the duty of the Commissioner of Public Health and Safety to
serve or cause to be served a notice in writing upon the owner, agent, occupant
or person in possession or charge of any premises on which weeds or plants are
permitted to grow in violation of the provisions of this subchapter an to
demand the abatement of the nuisance within five days.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.44)  (Ord. VG06-407, passed 6-22-2006)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
§ 9.20.310  FAILURE TO ABATE NUISANCE; ACTION BY VILLAGE.
   If the person so served with a notice as set forth in §
9.20.305 does not abate the nuisance within five days after the notice, the
Commissioner of Public Health and Safety shall cause the summary abatement of
the nuisance. Summary abatement may be caused by the employment of private
contractors or the use of the village equipment and personnel. If private
contractors are utilized for this purpose, the Commission of Public Health and
Safety shall keep an account of the expense thereof, and the expense shall be
charged to and paid by the owner or occupant. If the village’s equipment and
personnel are utilized, the Commissioner of Public Health and Safety shall keep
an account of the expense thereof, with minimum charge of $35 per hour for
labor and an additional charge for any village equipment which is used. The
expense shall be charged to and paid by the owner or occupant.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.44)  (Ord. VG06-407, passed 6-22-2006)
§ 9.20.315  LIEN FOR WEED REMOVAL; NOTICE.
   (A)   Charges for the weed removal shall be a lien upon the premises.
Whenever a bill for the charges remains unpaid for ten days after it has been
rendered, the Clerk may file with the Recorder of Deeds of the county, a
statement of lien claim. This statement shall contain the legal description of
the premises, the expenses and costs incurred, and the date the weeds were cut,
and a notice the village claims a lien for this amount.
   (B)   Notice of the lien claim shall be mailed to the owner of the premises
if his or her address is known; provided, however, that failure of the Clerk to
record the lien claim or to mail the notice, or the failure of the owner to
receive the notice shall not affect the right to foreclose the lien for the
charges as provided in §
9.20.320.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.44)  (Ord. VG06-407, passed 6-22-2006)
§ 9.20.320  FORECLOSURE OF LIEN.
   (A)   Property subject to a lien for unpaid weed cutting charges shall be
sold for nonpayment of the same and the proceeds of the sale shall be applied
to pay the charges after deducting costs, as is the case with the foreclosure
of statutory liens. The foreclosure shall be in equity in the name of the
village.
   (B)   The Village Attorney is authorized and directed to institute the
proceedings in the name of the village in any court having jurisdiction over
the matter against any property for which the bill has remained unpaid ten days
after it has been rendered, or at the time as he or she may be so directed by
the Council.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.44)  (Ord. VG06-407, passed 6-22-2006)
§ 9.20.325  COLLECTION PROCEDURES; ATTORNEY’S FEES.
   In addition to the remedies set forth above, the village may also file an
action in the Grundy County Circuit Court for the recovery of any expenses
incurred herein by the village in abating any nuisance. The action may be filed
independently of, or in addition to, any lien claim, foreclosure proceeding or
other proceeding instituted by the village. In addition to the recovery of
costs for labor and equipment for the abatement of any nuisance, the village
shall also be entitled to recover its court costs and reasonable attorney’s
fees incurred therewith.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.44)  (Ord. VG06-407, passed 6-22-2006)
§ 9.20.330  JOINT AND SEVERAL LIABILITY.
   (A)   Both the owner and occupant shall be jointly and severally liable for
the payment and satisfaction of all costs incurred by the village in any way
related to the abatement of any nuisance.
   (B)   Costs include, but are not limited to, recording costs, court costs,
filing fees, deposition expenses, subpoena fees, travel charges, copy and fax
charges, expert witness fees, postage costs and other similar expenses.
   (C)   In addition, the owner and occupant shall be jointly and severally
liable for the payment and satisfaction of all reasonable attorney’s fees
incurred by the village in any way related to the abatement of any nuisance,
whether incurred with or without a lawsuit or whether incurred with our without
the recording of a lien.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.44)  (Ord. VG06-407, passed 6-22-2006)
SIGNS AND NOTICES
§ 9.20.350  UNAUTHORIZED SIGNS AND NOTICES ON PUBLIC PROPERTY PROHIBITED.
   (A)   It is unlawful for any person to erect, set up, post or affix in any
manner to or upon public property, including but not limited to village
buildings, fences, poles or upon any utility pole located upon village
property, any sign, bill, poster, notice or other drawing or writing without
the prior permission of the Village Council.
   (B)   The Village Council may, by resolution, authorize the Mayor to issue
permits for the signs and notices, from time to time.
(Ord. G-119, passed 8-22-1988)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
§ 9.20.355  UNAUTHORIZED SIGNS AND NOTICES ON PRIVATE PROPERTY PROHIBITED.
   It is unlawful for any person to erect, set up, post or affix in any manner
to or upon any wall, fence or other private property within the village limits
any sign, bill, poster, notice or other drawing or writing without the prior
permission of the owner thereof or other person having authority to consent to
the same.
(Ord. G-119, passed 8-22-1988)  Penalty, see §
9.20.999
§ 9.20.360  REMOVAL OF VIOLATIONS.
   (A)   The Commissioner of Public Health and Safety shall, from time to time,
cause all items in violation of this subchapter to be removed by village
employees from village property and destroyed.
   (B)   Upon authorization from any property owner, he or she may cause all
the items in violation of this subchapter to be removed from the private
property within the village.
(Ord. G-119, passed 8-22-1988)
§ 9.20.999  PENALTY.
   (A)   General. Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which
no specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
1.05.999.
   (B)   Abandoned refrigerators. Any person, firm or corporation violating any
provision of §
9.20.005 shall be fined not less than $75 nor more than $750 for each offense,
and a separate offense shall be deemed committed on each day during or on which
a violation occurs or continues.
(Prior Code, § 8.04.020)
   (C)   Bonfires. Any person, firm or corporation violating any provision of §
9.20.015 shall be fined not less than $75 nor more than $750 for each offense,
and a separate offense shall be deemed committed on each day during or on which
a violation occurs or continues.
(Prior Code, § 8.08.020)
   (D)   Contagious diseases. Any person, firm or corporation violating any of
the provisions of §§
9.20.030 through
9.20.050 or violating any of the reasonable rules of the Commissioner of Public
Safety with regard to quarantined premises or disturbing or disregarding any
notice of quarantine placed by or under the direction of the Commissioner of
Public Safety shall be fined not less than $75 nor more than $750 for each
offense, and a separate offense shall be deemed committed on each day during
which or on which a violation occurs or continues.
(Prior Code, § 8.12.060)
   (E)   Explosives. Any person possessing, manufacturing, using, transporting
or storing explosives in violation of §
9.20.070 shall be fined not less than $75 nor more than $750 and a separate
offense shall be deemed committed during or on which a violation occurs or
continues.
(Prior Code, § 8.16.020)
   (F)   Fireworks. Any person or corporation violating any provision of §§
9.20.085 through
9.20.100 shall be fined not less than $75 nor more than $750 for each offense
and a separate offense shall be deemed committed on each day during or on which
a violation occurs or continues.
(Prior Code, § 8.20.050)
   (G)   Flammable liquid storage. Any person storing the liquids in violation
of §
9.20.115 shall be fined not less than $75 nor more than $750 for each offense
and a separate offense shall be deemed committed during or on which a violation
occurs or continues.
(Prior Code, § 8.24.020)
   (H)   Food dealers; generally. Any person, firm or corporation violating any
provisions of §§
9.20.130 through
9.20.145 shall be fined not less than $75 nor more than $750 for each offense,
and a separate offense shall be deemed committed on each day during or on which
a violation occurs or continues.
(Prior Code, § 8.28.050)
   (I)   Restaurants. Any person, firm or corporation violating any provision
of §§
9.20.160 through
9.20.165 shall be fined not less than $75 nor more than $750 for each offense,
and a separate offense shall be deemed committed on each day during or on which
a violation occurs or continues.
(Prior Code, § 8.32.030)
   (J)   Scavenging of recyclable materials from curbside recycling bins. Any
person, company, firm or corporation violating any of the provisions of §
9.20.240 shall be punished by a fine or not less than $75 nor more than $750.
   (K)   Nuisances. Any person, firm or corporation violating any provision of
§§
9.20.260 through
9.20.275 shall be fined not less than $75 nor more than $750 for each offense,
and a separate offense shall be deemed committed on each and every day during
or on which a violation occurs or is permitted to continue.
(Prior Code, § 8.40.040)
   (L)   Prohibiting certain nuisances.  Any person who violates any provision
of §
9.20.275 shall upon conviction be fined not less than $75 nor more than $750.
Each hour during which a violation occurs shall be deemed a separate and
distinct offense.
   (M)   Plants and weeds.  In addition to the lien remedy in §§
9.20.290 through
9.20.330, any person who fails to abate a weed nuisance within five days of the
notice provided for in §
9.20.305 shall be fined not less than $75 nor more than $750, and a separate
offense shall be deemed committed on each day during or on which the nuisance
remains unabated.
(Prior Code, Chapter 8.44)
   (N)   Signs and notices.  Any person, firm or corporation violating any
provision of §§
9.20.350 through
9.20.360 shall be fined not less than $75 nor more than $750 for each offense,
and a separate offense shall be deemed committed on each day during or on which
a violation occurs or continues.
(Ord. G-119, passed 8-22-1988; Ord. G-122, passed 3-12-1989; Ord. G-135, passed
4-10-1995; Ord. VG06-407, passed 6-22-2006)
CHAPTER 9.25: PARKS AND RECREATION
Section
   
9.25.005   Closing times for parks
   
9.25.010   Authorizing the use of village owned picnic tables
   
9.25.015   Parks and school within village safe zone
§ 9.25.005  CLOSING TIMES FOR PARKS.
   (A)   For the purpose of this section, the following definitions shall
apply.
      DUSK.  The time of day immediately following sunset.
      PARK.  Any village owned play field, pool, pond, recreation center,
playground or any other area or property devoted to active or passive
recreation.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person to go or be in or upon any village
park from dusk until sunrise.
   (C)   It shall be unlawful for any vehicle to be parked in a village park
from dusk until sunrise.
   (D)   The Director of Public Works is hereby authorized and directed to
purchase and install any and all necessary signs to implement the provisions of
this section and to provide adequate notice regarding the regulations contained
herein.
(Ord. VG04-388, passed 7-26-2004)  Penalty, see §
1.05.999
§ 9.25.010  AUTHORIZING THE USE OF VILLAGE OWNED PICNIC TABLES.
   (A)   The Village of Gardner will allow the use of the Village of Gardner
picnic tables to residents of the Village of Gardner for use within the
corporate limits of the Village of Gardner upon the following conditions:
      (1)   Requests for use of the picnic tables shall be placed on the agenda
at a Village Council meeting prior to the date the tables will be borrowed;
      (2)   The tables shall be loaned on a first come/first serve basis;
      (3)   A damage deposit shall be required in the amount of $150 per table
borrowed;
      (4)   In the event there is any damage to the tables including defacing
of the tables, that the deposit on the table will be immediately forfeited and
the resident shall be permitted to retain the damaged or defaced table;
      (5)   The tables will be loaned for no more than a three-day period;
      (6)   The tables shall not be loaned during the Gardner Days celebration;
      (7)   The village resident shall sign a receipt at the time of picking up
the tables verifying the condition of the tables; and
      (8)   It is requested that the village resident who borrows the tables
make a donation to the Gardner Days Fund as consideration for the use of the
Village of Gardner picnic tables.
   (B)   This section shall be published in pamphlet form and shall be in full
force and effect from and after its passage, approval and publication as
required by law.
(Ord. M-244, passed 5-22-1995)
§ 9.25.015  PARKS AND SCHOOL WITHIN VILLAGE SAFE ZONE.
   (A)   The Village of Gardner supports and enforces the enhanced penalties of
the state criminal laws for activities that occur within school zones or within
1,000 feet of the school zone.
   (B)   The Village of Gardner hereby declares all parks and schools within
the village limits to be safe zones as protected by the Illinois Criminal Code
and that these areas shall be monitored with particular scrutiny and that the
Village of Gardner shall seek to enforce the aforementioned provisions by all
means at its disposal.
(Res. 177, passed 5-23-1994)

CHAPTER 11.05: LICENSES AND PERMITS
Section
   
11.05.005   Applications
   
11.05.010   Forms
   
11.05.015   Signatures
   
11.05.020   Investigations
   
11.05.025   Fees
   
11.05.030   Termination of licenses
   
11.05.035   Buildings and premises; compliance with village requirements
   
11.05.040   Revocation of licenses
   
11.05.045   Posting of licenses
 
   
11.05.999   Penalty
§ 11.05.005  APPLICATIONS.
   (A)   Applications for all licenses and permits required by ordinance shall
be made in writing to the Village Clerk in the absence of provision to the
contrary.
   (B)   Each application shall state the name of the applicant, the permit or
license desired, the location to be used, if any, the time covered and the fee
to be paid.
   (C)   Each application shall contain additional information as may be needed
for the proper guidance of the village officials in the issuing of the permit
or license applied for.
(Prior Code, § 5.04.010)
§ 11.05.010  FORMS.
   Forms for all licenses and permits, and applications therefor, shall be
prepared and kept on file by the Village Clerk.
(Prior Code, § 5.04.020)
§ 11.05.015  SIGNATURES.
   Each license or permit issued shall bear the signatures of the Mayor and the
Clerk in the absence of any provision to the contrary.
(Prior Code, § 5.04.030)
§ 11.05.020  INVESTIGATIONS.
   (A)   Upon the receipt of an application for a license or permit where the
ordinance of the village necessitates an inspection or investigation before the
issuance of the permit or license, the Village Clerk shall refer the
application to the proper officer for making the investigation within 48 hours
of the time of the receipt.
   (B)   The officer charged with the duty of making the investigation or
inspection shall make a report thereon, favorable or otherwise, within ten days
after receiving the application or a copy thereof.
(Prior Code, § 5.04.040)
§ 11.05.025  FEES.
   (A)   In the absence of provision to the contrary, all fees and charges for
licenses or permits shall be paid in advance when the application therefor is
made to the Village Clerk.
   (B)   When application for an annual license is made after the expiration of
six months of the current license year, the license for the remainder of the
year shall be issued upon payment of one-half of the annual fee.
(Prior Code, § 5.04.050)
§ 11.05.030  TERMINATION OF LICENSES.
   (A)   All annual licenses shall terminate on the last day of the fiscal year
of the village in which they are issued where no provision to the contrary is
made.
   (B)   The Village Clerk shall mail to all licensees of the village a
statement of the time of expiration of the license held by the licensee, if an
annual one, three weeks prior to the date of the expiration; provided, that a
failure to send out the notice, or the failure of the licensee to receive it,
shall not excuse the licensee from a failure to obtain a new license, or a
renewal, nor shall it be a defense in an action for operating without a
license.
(Prior Code, § 5.04.060)
§ 11.05.035  BUILDINGS AND PREMISES; COMPLIANCE WITH VILLAGE REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   No license shall be issued for the conduct of any business, and no
permit for any thing or act, if the premises and building to be used for the
purpose do not fully comply with the requirements of the village.
   (B)   No license or permit shall be issued for the conduct of any business
or performance of any act which would involve a violation of
Chapter 15.15 of this code.
(Prior Code, § 5.04.070)
§ 11.05.040  REVOCATION OF LICENSES.
   (A)   Any license or permit for a limited time may be revoked by the Mayor
at any time during the life of the license or permit for any violation by the
licensee or permittee of the ordinance provisions relating to the license or
permit, the subject matter of the license or permit, or to the premises
occupied.
   (B)   The revocation may be in addition to any fine imposed.
(Prior Code, § 5.04.080)
§ 11.05.045  POSTING OF LICENSES.
   It shall be the duty of any person conducting a licensed business in the
village to keep his or her license posted in a prominent place on the premises
used for the business at all times.
(Prior Code, § 5.04.090)
§ 11.05.999  PENALTY.
   Any person, firm or corporation violating any provision of this chapter
shall be fined not less than $75 nor more than $750 for each offense, and a
separate offense shall be deemed committed on each day during or on which a
violation occurs or continues.
(Prior Code, § 5.04.100)
CHAPTER 11.10: ALCOHOLIC LIQUOR DEALERS
